Defending Abu Bakr's Request to Be Relieved
Baqillani answers the objection that Abu Bakr's request for relief shows unfitness.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why Abu Bakr's request to be relieved of office does not indicate unfitness, and how Baqillani defends it through piety and the concept of a test.

Core Idea
Abu Bakr’s request to be relieved reflects humility, not unfitness.

Some object that Abu Bakr's plea 'Relieve me' proves he was unworthy of the caliphate. Imam Baqillani responds by showing that such a request is actually a sign of piety and caution. Moreover, it may have been a deliberate test to distinguish true supporters. This passage clarifies how prophetic excellence and leadership can coexist with apparent reluctance.

Guided Path
1
Read the Objection and Answer
Read the Arabic passage and its translation carefully. Notice how the objection is framed and how Baqillani begins his response.
The objectors use Abu Bakr's own words against him.
2
Identify the Two Arguments
Baqillani gives two lines of defense: first, that the request shows piety and proper caution; second, that it was a test of the community. Identify where each argument starts.
The second argument is attributed to those who believe in textual designation (nass).
3
Reflect on the Deeper Principles
Consider how Baqillani uses the concept of virtue and intention to turn an apparent weakness into strength. This shows a key principle in kalam: defensive arguments can reinterpret evidence favorably.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فإن قالوا : كيف يكون أبو بكر مستحقاً لهذا الأمر وهو يقول: «أقيلوني أقيلوني»؟ قيل لهم : ليس في استقالته من تحمل ثقل الإمامة لفضل دينه وخشيته وورَعِه ما يُقعده عن استحقاقها وما ينبغي لفاضل عُرضت عليه أن يظهر المسارعة إليها والسرور بها ؛ فإن ذلك مُلْقٍ له في الظَّنَّة ومُورّط للقوم في التهمة فما قال من ذلك إلى ما يقوله مثله في الفضل والتقدم ولو أقالوه وولوا غيره لكان جائزاً وقد قال القائلون بالنص على إمامته : إنه إنما أراد بهذا القول وبقوله : وليتكم ولست بخيركم امتحان القوم ليرى من يقبل هذا القول ليعرف بذلك المطيع من العاصي وقابل النص عليه من الراد له فيقومه بما يقوم مثله به قالوا وهذا بمنزلة قول عمر لحذيفة
If they say: 'How can Abu Bakr be worthy of this matter while he says: “Relieve me, relieve me”?' It is said to them: There is nothing in his asking to be relieved from bearing the burden of the imamate, due to the virtue of his religion, his fear (of God), and his piety, that disqualifies him from being worthy of it. It is not befitting for a virtuous person offered something to show haste towards it and delight in it, for that would cast him into suspicion and embroil the people in accusation. So he said what he said of that, similar to what one like him in virtue and precedence would say. And if they had relieved him and appointed someone else, it would have been permissible. And those who advocate the textual designation (nass) for his imamate have said: He only meant by this statement and by his saying 'I have been put in charge of you while I am not the best of you' to test the people to see who accepts this saying, so that thereby he might know the obedient from the disobedient, and the one who accepts the designation from the one who rejects it, and then he would punish him with what is appropriate. They said: This is similar to the statement of Umar to Hudhayfa.
Source pages p. 498

Commentary
This passage is another objection-and-answer unit. The objectors argue: Abu Bakr's request to be relieved ('Aqiluni') shows he is not fit for the caliphate. Baqillani responds with a two-part argument. First, he explains that such a request is actually a sign of virtue: because of his piety and fear of God, Abu Bakr did not want to appear eager for power, since eagerness would cause suspicion and accusation. Thus, his request is proper behavior for a virtuous person. If they had relieved him, it would have been permissible. Second, another interpretation (from those who believe in textual designation) is that Abu Bakr's words were a test to distinguish the obedient from the disobedient and to identify those who accept or reject the divine designation. This is compared to a similar test by Umar with Hudhayfa. The answer as a whole defends Abu Bakr's worthiness by showing that his words are consistent with excellence and could be a deliberate test.

Key Terms
أقيلوني
الإمامة
النص
امتحان

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some think Abu Bakr's request to be relieved indicates he was unfit or unwilling to lead.
Correction: Baqillani shows that the request reflects pious humility and could be a test of the community, not a sign of unfitness.

Key Takeaway
Abu Bakr's request for relief is defended as a sign of piety and a possible test, not as a disqualification from leadership.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you are offered a position of responsibility, does your heart immediately leap with joy and eagerness? How does Abu Bakr’s example challenge you to examine the purity of your intentions? Will you now pause and consider whether your eagerness might be a sign of hidden pride?
?
Think of a time you were tested by someone in authority to see your obedience. Did you pass or fail? Now consider that Allah tests you daily in ways you may not recognize. After reading that Abu Bakr’s words were a test, are you ready to be tested by the example of the Companions? What will you change today?
?
You often claim to love the Sahaba, but when you read that Abu Bakr asked to be relieved, do you secretly think it was a weakness? Search your heart: have you ever judged a believer for showing humility or reluctance to lead? Will you now repent and see such actions as signs of virtue?

Baqillani's Refutation: Three Meanings of Abu Bakr's Saying
Baqillani offers three interpretations of Abu Bakr's saying to refute Shi'a objections.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the three interpretations Baqillani offers for Abu Bakr's saying 'I am not the best of you' and how they refute the Shi'a objection to his caliphate.

Core Idea
Abu Bakr's humility proves, not disproves, the legitimacy of his imamate.

Imam Baqillani addresses a key Shi'a objection: if Abu Bakr said he was not the best, how could he be caliph? He shows that Abu Bakr's words can be understood in multiple pious ways, each of which actually supports his right to leadership. This passage is a classic example of Sunni kalam defending the early caliphate.

Guided Path
1
Understand the Context
Read the opening lines which connect the issue to the hadith 'الأئمة من قريش' and the argument against lineage as a criterion.
Notice that Baqillani immediately grounds the discussion in a Prophetic hadith.
2
First Interpretation: Human Fallibility
Identify the first interpretation: Abu Bakr acknowledges his own forgetfulness and error to refute the claim that only an infallible can be imam.
This interpretation emphasizes that imamate does not require عصمة (infallibility).
3
Second Interpretation: Leadership as Divine Favor
Understand the second interpretation: Abu Bakr means that God's appointment made him imam, obligating obedience to him and freeing him from obeying others.
This highlights that imamate is a divine favor, not a measure of personal virtue.
4
Third Interpretation and Supporting Example
Review the third interpretation: Abu Bakr may have recognized someone more virtuous but chose himself due to consensus and suitability. Then see how he applied this principle by nominating Umar and Abu Ubayda.
This demonstrates the permissibility of imamate of the less virtuous when necessary.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وعشيرة ولأن بني هاشم أعلى منه في ذِرْوَةِ النسب لكي يدلهم بذلك على أن هذا الأمر العظيم ليس يُستحق بعلو النسب، وأنه ليس بمقصور على بني هاشم دون غيرهم من قريش بظاهر قوله عليه السلام : «الأئمة من قريش». ويمكن أن يكون أراد بقوله : وليتكم ولست بخيركم» أي إنه يجوز علي من السهو والغلط ووساوس الصدور وخواطر النفوس ما يجوز من السهو عليكم لكي يدلّهم بذلك على فساد قول من زعم أن هذا الأمر لا يستحقه إلا الوافر المعصوم. ويمكن أن يكون أراد بقوله: «وليتكم ولست بخيركم لولا أن الله فضلني عليكم بحق الولاية فأوجب عليكم من طاعتي أن صرت إماماً وأسقط عني فرض طاعتكم ويمكن أيضاً أن يكون قد اعتقد أن في الأمة أفضل منه إلا أن الكلمة عليه أجمعُ والأمةَ بنظره أصلحُ لكي يدلهم على جواز إمامة المفضول عند عارض يمنع من نصب الفاضل ولهذا ما قال للأنصار وغيرهم : قد رضيت لكم أحد هذين الرجلين فبايعوا أحدهما عمر بن الخطاب وأبا عبيدة بن الجراح وهو يعلم أن أبا عبيدة دونه ودون عثمان وعلي في الفضل غير أنه قد رأى أن الكلمة تجتمع عليه وتنحَسِمُ الفتنة بنظره وهذا أيضاً مما لا جواب لهم عنه
And [his] clan, and because the Banu Hashim are higher than him in the peak of lineage, to thereby indicate to them that this great matter is not deserved by nobility of lineage, and that it is not restricted to Banu Hashim to the exclusion of other Quraysh, by the apparent meaning of his statement, peace be upon him: 'The leaders are from Quraysh.' And it is possible that he meant by his statement 'I have become your leader and I am not the best of you' that there occurs from me of forgetfulness and error and whispers of the breasts and thoughts of the souls what occurs of forgetfulness from you, to thereby indicate to them the invalidity of the saying of those who claim that this matter is only deserved by the completely infallible. And it is possible that he meant by his statement: 'I have become your leader and I am not the best of you, except that God has preferred me over you by the right of leadership, so He made obligatory upon you from obedience to me that I became an imam and He dropped from me the obligation of obeying you.' And it is also possible that he believed that there is in the community one better than him, except that the consensus is upon him and the community, in his view, is more suitable, to thereby indicate to them the permissibility of the imamate of the less virtuous when there is an obstacle that prevents the appointment of the more virtuous. For this reason, he said to the Ansar and others: 'I have approved for you one of these two men, so pledge allegiance to one of them: Umar ibn al-Khattab and Abu Ubayda ibn al-Jarrah,' while knowing that Abu Ubayda is inferior to him and inferior to Uthman and Ali in virtue, except that he saw that consensus would unite upon him and sedition would be cut off by his appointment. And this, too, is something they have no answer for.
Source pages p. 498

Commentary
This passage is a refutation of a Shi'a objection to Abu Bakr's caliphate based on his reported saying 'وليتكم ولست بخيركم' (I have become your leader and I am not the best of you). Baqillani begins by connecting the issue to the hadith 'الأئمة من قريش' (the leaders are from Quraysh) to show that nobility is not the criterion. Then he provides three possible interpretations of Abu Bakr's saying that neutralize the objection. First: Abu Bakr was acknowledging his own human fallibility, arguing against those who claim only an infallible (معصوم) can be imam. Second: he meant that God's favor in appointing him as imam made obedience to him obligatory and freed him from obeying others. Third: he may have recognized someone more virtuous but chose himself because consensus was on him and he was more suitable, teaching the permissibility of imamate of the less virtuous. Baqillani supports this with Abu Bakr's nomination of Umar and Abu Ubayda, knowing their relative merit. He concludes that this argument is unanswerable.

Key Terms
إمامة
ولاية
عصمة
مفضول
فاضل
سهو
نص

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Abu Bakr's statement 'I am not the best of you' proves he was not fit for the caliphate.
Correction: Baqillani shows that the statement can be interpreted in ways that actually support his imamate, such as acknowledging human fallibility to reject infallibility condition, or showing that leadership is a divine favor, or allowing imamate of the less virtuous for the sake of unity.

Checkpoint
What is one of the interpretations Baqillani gives for Abu Bakr's statement 'I am not the best of you'?
A) He was admitting he was unqualified for leadership.
B) He was showing humility and that imamate does not require infallibility.
C) He was forced to say it by the Companions.
D) He was lying to test the people.

Key Takeaway
Baqillani's three interpretations defend Abu Bakr's caliphate by showing his statement can be understood in ways consistent with Sunni theology.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When have you used your own perceived flaws as an excuse to avoid responsibility, unlike Abu Bakr who led despite acknowledging his imperfections? Will you stop hiding behind your weaknesses and step up where God has placed you?
?
Do you secretly believe that only the 'perfect' can lead—whether in your family, community, or workplace? How does Baqillani's argument expose your own fear of taking initiative when you are not the most qualified?
?
Baqillani shows that unity can be more important than having the 'best' leader. Where in your life have you prioritized your own preference for the 'best' over maintaining unity? Will you commit to supporting the leadership that brings people together, even if it is not your ideal choice?

Baqillani on Abu Bakr's Request to Be Relieved
Baqillani refutes the objection that Abu Bakr's request to be relieved proves his unfitness.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how Baqillani refutes the objection that Abu Bakr's plea to be relieved proves his unfitness for the caliphate, showing it indicates piety and was a test of the community.

Core Idea
A leader's request to be relieved can reflect piety, not inability.

The objection that Abu Bakr's plea to be relieved shows his unfitness is a common critique against the legitimacy of his caliphate. Imam Baqillani addresses this by reinterpreting the request as a sign of religious fear and testing the community's obedience. This passage reveals how kalam reasoning defends the first caliph's right to leadership.

Guided Path
1
Understand the objection
The objectors say: How can Abu Bakr be worthy of the imamate when he said 'Relieve me, relieve me'? Recognize that this objection assumes that a request to step down implies unfitness.
This is the challenge Baqillani responds to.
2
Read Baqillani's direct response
Read the first part of the passage where Baqillani argues that such a request reflects Abu Bakr's religiosity, fear, and piety, not disqualification. A virtuous person should not show eagerness for power.
Note the reasoning: eagerness would cast suspicion.
3
Examine the alternative interpretation (nass)
Those who assert textual designation (nass) for Ali offer a different interpretation: Abu Bakr's words were a test to distinguish the obedient from the disobedient. Consider how this transforms the meaning of the request.
Baqillani presents this as a plausible interpretation, not necessarily his own.
4
Connect to the analogy with Umar and Hudhayfa
Baqillani compares this to Umar's question to Hudhayfa about hypocrisy. Umar knew he wasn't a hypocrite but asked to test. Similarly, Abu Bakr's statement was a test, not a confession.
This analogy strengthens the argument that the request was a test.

فإن قالوا : كيف يكون أبو بكر مستحقاً لهذا الأمر وهو يقول: «أقيلوني أقيلوني؟ . قيل لهم : ليس في استقالته من تحمل ثقل الإمامة لفضل دينه وخشيته وورَعِه ما يُقعده عن استحقاقها وما ينبغي لفاضل عُرضت عليه أن يظهر المسارعة إليها والسرور بها ؛ فإن ذلك مُلْقٍ له في الظَّنَّة ومُورّط للقوم في التهمة فما قال من ذلك إلى ما يقوله مثله في الفضل والتقدم ولو أقالوه وولوا غيره لكان جائزاً وقد قال القائلون بالنص على إمامته : إنه إنما أراد بهذا القول وبقوله : وليتكم ولست بخيركم امتحان القوم ليرى من يقبل هذا القول ليعرف بذلك المطيع من العاصي وقابل النص عليه من الراد له فيقومه بما يقوم مثله به قالوا وهذا بمنزلة قول عمر لحذيفة لما قال إن رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم عرفه المنافقين: نشدتك بالله هل أنا منهم؟» فقال: «لا، ولا أخبِرُ بعدك أحداً» ، وقد علم أن عمر لم يشك في إيمانه وأنه ليس بمنافق يعلم ذلك نفسه فلا معنى من الاستعلامه حال نفسه من حذيفة وإنما قال ذلك امتحاناً ليعلم صدقه من كذبه وهذا أيضاً ليس ببعيد في التأويل
If they say: How can Abu Bakr be deserving of this matter while he says: 'Relieve me, relieve me?' It is said to them: There is not in his request to be relieved from bearing the burden of the imamate, due to his religiousness, fear, and piety, anything that disqualifies him from deserving it, and it is not befitting for a virtuous person to whom such a matter is presented to show haste towards it and delight in it, for that would cast him into suspicion and implicate the people in accusation. What he said is not beyond what someone like him in virtue and precedence would say. And if they had relieved him and appointed someone else, it would have been permissible. And those who assert the textual designation (nass) of his imamate have said: He intended by this statement and by his statement 'I have become your leader and I am not the best of you' to test the people, to see who would accept this statement, so that thereby he would know the obedient from the disobedient and the one who accepts the designation from the one who rejects it, and he would deal with them accordingly. They said: This is like the statement of Umar to Hudhayfa when he said that the Messenger of God had informed him of the hypocrites: 'I adjure you by God, am I among them?' He replied: 'No, and I will not inform anyone after you.' And he knew that Umar did not doubt his faith and that he was not a hypocrite, knowing that himself, so there is no meaning for him to ask about his own state from Hudhayfa. Rather, he said that as a test to know his truth from his falsehood. And this, too, is not far-fetched in interpretation.
Source pages p. 498

Commentary
This passage is a refutation of an objection based on Abu Bakr's request to be relieved ('أقيلوني أقيلوني'). Baqillani argues that such a request shows piety and fear of responsibility, not inability. A virtuous person should not rush to power. Additionally, those who advocate textual designation (النص) of Ali offer a different interpretation: Abu Bakr was testing the people to see who accepts him. Baqillani equates this to Umar's question to Hudhayfa about hypocrisy—Umar knew he was not a hypocrite but asked to test. Similarly, Abu Bakr's words were a test, not a confession of unfitness.

Misconception: That Abu Bakr's request to be relieved proves he was unfit for the caliphate.
Correction: Baqillani shows that the request reflects piety and fear of responsibility, not unfitness. Alternatively, it was a test of the community's obedience.

Why does Baqillani argue that Abu Bakr's request to be relieved does not disqualify him?

Baqillani refutes the objection by showing that Abu Bakr's request to be relieved indicates piety and was a test, not a confession of unfitness.

?
Consider a time when someone doubted your intentions or abilities. How did you respond? If you were in Abu Bakr's position, would you have been willing to let others test your sincerity through your own words? What does his test teach you about relying on God's judgment rather than human opinion?

Abu Bakr's request to be relieved could have been misunderstood as weakness. Are there areas of your life where you avoid doing the right thing because you fear being misunderstood? How can you draw courage from his example to act with piety and trust that God knows your heart, regardless of how others perceive you?

Refuting the 'Faltatan' Objection Against Abu Bakr
Baqillani refutes the objection from Umar's 'faltatan' remark by reductio ad absurdum.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand Baqillani's refutation of the claim that Umar's statement about Abu Bakr's allegiance being a 'faltatan' undermines its legitimacy, and how he shows that the statement actually supports the caliphate's continuity.

Core Idea
Umar's 'faltatan' remark does not delegitimize Abu Bakr; it affirms his own imamate.

In this passage, Baqillani addresses an objection from those who cite Umar's famous statement that the allegiance to Abu Bakr was a 'faltatan' (a sudden event) that God protected from evil. Critics argue this shows Abu Bakr's caliphate was illegitimate. Baqillani counters by showing that if that were true, it would make Umar's own caliphate—which came through Abu Bakr's appointment—equally invalid, which is absurd. Instead, the statement must be understood in its proper context.

Guided Path
1
Understand the objection
The critic points to Umar's statement calling Abu Bakr's allegiance a 'faltatan' and his order to kill anyone who repeats such an act. This is the challenge Baqillani must answer.
Notice the critic uses Umar's own words against the Sunni position.
2
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage once and then the translation. Pay attention to Baqillani's initial premise that no one doubts Umar's sanity, and follow his logical argument step by step.
3
Follow Baqillani's reductio ad absurdum
Baqillani argues that if Abu Bakr's allegiance were invalid, then Umar's own imamate (based on Abu Bakr's appointment) would also be invalid, leading to the absurd conclusion that Umar himself should be killed.
This is a classic logical argument: assume the objection is true, then derive a contradiction.
4
Examine the contextual interpretation
Baqillani explains that Umar said this when entrusting the consultation (shura) to the community, not to deny legitimacy. He also notes Umar's own praise of Abu Bakr contradicts any real disapproval.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فإن قالوا : كيف يكون أبو بكر مستحقاً لهذا الأمر وعمر يقول قولاً ظاهراً على المنبر: ألا إن بيعة أبي بكر كانت فلتةً وقى الله شرها وأمر بقتل من عاد إلى مثلها بقوله في هذا الخبر: فمن عاد إلى مثلها فاقتلوه»؟ قيل لهم : ما شككنا في شيء فإنا لا نشك وإياكم في أن عمر عمر لم يكن مجنوناً ولا مخلطاً وهذا الكلام إن حُمِلَ على ما قلتم صار في حكم الجنون من قائله لأن عمر كان يحتج على الناس في إثبات إمامته والدعاء إلى طاعته والانقياد له في الإمامة بعقد أبي بكر له الأمر وعهده إليه فيه وإذا كانت بيعـة أبي بكر باطلة يجب قتل صاحبها ومن عاد إلى مثلها وجب أن يكون عهده إلى عمر باطلاً كعهد أبي بكر وموجبا لقتل عمر وقتل من نظر في أمور المسلمين بعدهم من فكان أن تقول له الصحابة : فأنت أيضاً ممن يجب قتلك ولا يجب إمام العمل على عهدك في الشورى. وإنما قال هذا الكلام لما عهد إليهم في الشورى على المنبر وكان يجب أن يقال له أيضاً قد قلت فيمن هذا وصفه : ودِدْتُ أن أكون شعرة في صدره وما سابقته إلى خير قط إلا سبقني إليه
If they say: How can Abu Bakr be deserving of this matter while Umar says, explicitly from the pulpit: 'Indeed, the allegiance to Abu Bakr was a sudden event (faltatan) which God protected from evil,' and he ordered killing whoever returns to something like it, by his saying in this report: 'Whoever returns to something like it, kill him'? It is said to them: We have not doubted anything, for we and you do not doubt that Umar was not insane nor confused. And this speech, if interpreted as you claim, would become like madness from its speaker, because Umar used to argue [for others] in establishing his imamate and calling for his obedience and submission to his imamate by the contract of Abu Bakr for him and his covenant to him. If the allegiance of Abu Bakr was invalid, necessitating the killing of its participant and whoever returns to something like it, then it would be necessary that his covenant to Umar would be invalid, like the covenant of Abu Bakr, and necessitating the killing of Umar and the killing of those who look into the affairs of the Muslims after him. So the Companions would say to him: 'Then you also are among those whose killing is obligatory, and the imam should not be entrusted with action upon your covenant in the consultation (shura).' And he only said this speech when he entrusted to them the consultation from the pulpit. And it would have been necessary to say to him also: 'You have said about one with such description: "I wish I were a hair on his chest" and "I have not preceded him to any good except he preceded me to it."'
Source pages p. 499

Commentary
This passage refutes the objection using Umar's statement that Abu Bakr's allegiance was a 'فلتة' (sudden event). Baqillani argues that if it were truly invalid, Umar would be condemning his own imamate, since he assumed power through Abu Bakr's nomination. The logic: if Abu Bakr's allegiance is invalid, then his appointment of Umar is also invalid, and Umar himself would deserve killing. Since that is absurd, Umar's statement must be interpreted differently—he was referring to the informal nature of the pledge, not its illegitimacy, and he said it when entrusting the consultation to the community. Baqillani also notes that Umar made laudatory statements about Abu Bakr, such as wishing to be a hair on his chest, contradicting any real disapproval.

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Umar's phrase 'faltatan' proves that Abu Bakr's caliphate was illegitimate and a mistake.
Correction: Baqillani shows that if that were true, Umar's own imamate would be equally invalid, which is impossible; instead, the statement refers to the informal nature of the pledge and was made in a specific context.

C) He says Umar was not serious and later retracted.

Key Takeaway
Baqillani shows that Umar's 'faltatan' statement, when properly understood, actually supports the legitimacy of Abu Bakr's caliphate and Umar's own.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Have you ever dismissed a significant commitment or duty as a 'sudden mistake' to avoid the weight of responsibility? If Umar himself affirmed the value of that commitment, what excuse do you have?
?
Baqillani uses rigorous logic to defend Abu Bakr against a criticism that seems incriminating at face value. Where in your own life do you accept surface-level judgments about people or events without digging deeper? Will you commit to seeking the full truth before forming conclusions?
?
Umar's praise of Abu Bakr—wishing to be a hair on his chest—reveals deep humility. When was the last time you honestly admired someone you could have resented? Ask yourself: does your heart harbor hidden resentment toward those you publicly respect?

Defense of Abu Bakr's Caliphate Against Umar's Statement
Response to objection from Umar's 'falta' statement

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why Umar's statement about Abu Bakr's bay'ah being a 'falta' does not invalidate Abu Bakr's caliphate, and how the correct interpretation resolves the apparent contradiction.

Core Idea
Umar's 'falta' remark actually affirms Abu Bakr's unique merit and swift election.

This lesson addresses a common objection: Umar called Abu Bakr's bay'ah a 'falta' and ordered the killing of anyone who repeats it. How can this be reconciled with Sunni belief in Abu Bakr's rightful caliphate? Imam Baqillani provides a masterful defense, first showing that a literal reading leads to absurd self-contradiction, then offering the proper interpretation that aligns with Umar's consistent support of Abu Bakr.

Guided Path
1
Read the objection and the reductio
Read the first part of the passage where the opponent quotes Umar's statement and the author's response that a literal interpretation would imply Umar was insane.
Notice how the author uses the contradiction between Umar's words and his actions.
2
Understand the absurd consequence
If Umar's words are taken literally, then his own appointment by Abu Bakr would be invalid and he too would deserve death. This is used to reject the literal reading.
The author argues this would be inconsistent with Umar's own policies.
3
Learn the alternative interpretation
The author explains that 'falta' means done quickly without prolonged deliberation, not illegitimate. 'Protection from evil' refers to avoiding discord. The killing order applies to the Ansar's attempt to split the community, not to Abu Bakr.
Note how this interpretation is consistent with Umar's respect for Abu Bakr.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فإن قالوا : كيف يكون أبو بكر مستحقاً لهذا الأمر وعمر يقول قولاً ظاهراً على المنبر: ألا إن بيعة أبي بكر كانت فلتةً وقى الله شرها وأمر بقتل من عاد إلى مثلها بقوله في هذا الخبر: فمن عاد إلى مثلها فاقتلوه»؟ قيل لهم : ما شككنا في شيء فإنا لا نشك وإياكم في أن عمر عمر لم يكن مجنوناً ولا مخلطاً وهذا الكلام إن حُمِلَ على ما قلتم صار في حكم الجنون من قائله لأن عمر كان يحتج على الناس في إثبات إمامته والدعاء إلى طاعته والانقياد له في الإمامة بعقد أبي بكر له الأمر وعهده إليه فيه وإذا كانت بيعـة أبي بكر باطلة يجب قتل صاحبها ومن عاد إلى مثلها وجب أن يكون عهده إلى عمر باطلاً كعهد أبي بكر وموجبا لقتل عمر وقتل من نظر في أمور المسلمين بعدهم من فكان أن تقول له الصحابة : فأنت أيضاً ممن يجب قتلك ولا يجب يجب إمام العمل على عهدك في الشورى. وإنما قال هذا الكلام لما عهد إليهم في الشورى على المنبر وكان يجب أن يقال له أيضاً قد قلت فيمن هذا وصفه : ودِدْتُ أن أكون شعرة في صدره (٢) وما سابقته إلى خير قط إلا سبقني إليه (٣) وكان والله من خيرنا يوم توفي رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم، وأمثال هذه الأقاويل . وهذا الاختلال لا يتهم عمر به إلا مُخَلَّط جاهل . فإن قالوا فما معنى الخبر؟ قيل لهم : إن عُمَرَ كان يعتقد أن أبا بكر كان أفضل الأمة ومُبَرّزاً فيهم بالفضل وغير مُشتكل الأمر وأنه كان يستحق أخذها بالمناظرة عليها وأن من بعدها متقاربون في الرتبة والفضل لا يستحقونها على ذلك الوجه ؛ ولذلك جعلها شورى في ستة . وقوله «كانت فلتة» أي تمت على غير إعمال فكر ولا رويَّةٍ بل استوثقت فجاءةٌ. وقوله «وقى الله شرها»، يعني شر الخلاف عليها وشقّ العصا عند تمامها فإنه بعيد عنده أن ذلك مع ما رأى من تواثب الأنصار عليها واطلاع الفتنة رأسها وقوله «فمن عاد إلى مثلها فاقتلوه إنما أراد إلى مثل قول الأنصار وما حُكِيَ عن الأنصار من إرادتهم نصب إمامين في وقت واحد بقولهم: «منا أمير ومنكم أمير ولإخراجهم الأمر من قريش إلى غيرهم وهذان الأمران حرام فعلهما في الدين وجالبان الفتنة وإنما عَظَّمَ غلط الأنصار فيهما فقال لأهل الشورى وغيرهم لما عهد إليهم فيها : إن من عاد إلى مثل قول الأنصار فاقتلوه ويمكن أن يكون أراد من حاول أخذها بالمناظرة عليها وإظهار التقدم والتبريز بالفضل على وجه ما فعله أبو بكر وعُرف ذلك من أمره فاقتلوه ؛ لأنه لم يبق في هذه الأمة هذه منزلته . وإذا كان كذلك سقط ما تعلقوا به صح بهذه الجملة إمامة أبي بكر رضي الله عنه ونضّر وجهه.
If they say: How can Abu Bakr be deserving of this matter while Umar says openly on the pulpit: 'Indeed, the pledge of Abu Bakr was a sudden affair (falta); Allah protected [us] from its evil, and he ordered the killing of whoever returns to its like by his saying in this report: 'Whoever returns to its like, kill him'?' It is said to them: We do not doubt anything, for we and you do not doubt that Umar was not insane nor confused. This speech, if interpreted as you say, would become in the ruling of insanity from its speaker, because Umar used to argue to the people in establishing his imamah and calling them to obey him and submit to him in the imamah by the contract of Abu Bakr giving him the command and his bequest to him therein. And if the pledge of Abu Bakr was invalid, necessitating the killing of its doer and whoever returns to its like, then his bequest to Umar would be invalid like the bequest of Abu Bakr, necessitating the killing of Umar and the killing of whoever considered the affairs of the Muslims after them. So it would be that the Companions could say to him: You too are among those whose killing is obligatory, and the imam of action in your time in the consultation is not obligatory. But he said this speech when he bequeathed to them in the consultation on the pulpit, and it must be said to him also: You have said about one with this description: 'I wish I were a hair on his chest' and 'I never preceded him in good except he preceded me to it.' And he was, by Allah, among the best of us on the day the Messenger of Allah died, and similar statements. And this inconsistency is not attributed to Umar except by a confused ignorant person. Then if they say: What is the meaning of the report? It is said to them: Indeed, Umar believed that Abu Bakr was the best of the community, preeminent in virtue, and his affair was not problematic, and that he deserved to take it by deliberation over it, and that those after him were close in rank and virtue and did not deserve it in that manner; therefore he made it consultation among six. And his saying 'it was a sudden affair' means it was completed without employing thought nor consideration, but rather it was quickly secured. And his saying 'Allah protected [us] from its evil' means the evil of disagreement over it and the splitting of the stick at its completion, for it is far from him that this, with what he saw of the Ansar's rush toward it and the emergence of sedition at its head. And his saying 'Whoever returns to its like, kill him' only intended the like of the saying of the Ansar and what was narrated about the Ansar of their desire to appoint two imams at one time by their saying: 'An amir from us and an amir from you,' and their taking the matter out of Quraysh to others. These two matters are forbidden to do in the religion and bring about sedition. He emphasized the error of the Ansar in them and said to the people of consultation and others when he bequeathed to them: 'Whoever returns to the like of the saying of the Ansar, kill him.' It is possible that he intended whoever tried to take it by deliberation over it and showing precedence and excellence in virtue in the manner that Abu Bakr did, and that is known from his affair, then kill him, because no one in this community has this rank. And if this is the case, what they clung to falls away; by this summary the imamah of Abu Bakr is established, may Allah be pleased with him and brighten his face.
Source pages p. 499

Commentary
This passage is an extended response to an objection: How can Abu Bakr's caliphate be valid when Umar called it a 'falta' (sudden affair) and ordered the killing of anyone who attempted a similar seizure of power? The author first argues that to take Umar's words at face value would imply Umar was insane, since he himself later ruled by Abu Bakr's appointment. If Abu Bakr's pledge were invalid, then Umar's own appointment would be invalid and he too would deserve execution. This absurdity shows the objection must be mistaken. The author then provides a proper interpretation: Umar meant that the pledge was made swiftly without prolonged deliberation, not that it was illegitimate. 'Protection from evil' refers to avoiding the greater evil of discord and civil strife. The order to kill applies not to Abu Bakr's action but to those who would repeat the Ansar's attempt to split the community by appointing two imams or taking the caliphate out of Quraysh. Alternatively, it may apply to anyone who claimed to have the same unparalleled merit as Abu Bakr. With this explanation, the objection is refuted and Abu Bakr's imamah is affirmed.

شورى
إمامة
الأنصار

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some think Umar's 'falta' statement proves that Abu Bakr's caliphate was a mistake or invalid.
Correction: The author shows that Umar's words, properly understood, affirm Abu Bakr's swift election and unique merit, and the killing order refers to those who would cause division, not to Abu Bakr.

Checkpoint
According to the author, what is the intended meaning of Umar's statement that Abu Bakr's bay'ah was a 'falta'?
A) It was a forbidden act of rebellion.
B) It was completed swiftly without prolonged deliberation.
C) It was a secret agreement against the Ansar.
D) It was invalid and deserving of execution.

Key Takeaway
Umar's 'falta' remark, properly understood, affirms Abu Bakr's swift and unique election, not its illegitimacy.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Umar's words were misinterpreted by some as condemning the very leader he himself praised. Are there statements from scholars or leaders you have misunderstood or taken out of context? Will you commit to seeking correct understanding from reliable sources before making judgments?
?
The swift bay'ah of Abu Bakr prevented discord, yet some saw it as flawed. In your life, have you ever hesitated to support a clear good because it seemed sudden or unplanned? What can you learn from Umar's perspective that the swiftness was a mercy?
?
Umar acknowledged that no one had the same rank as Abu Bakr. Is there a person in your community—a parent, teacher, or friend—whom you have not fully appreciated for their unique contributions? How will you acknowledge their merit today, before it is too late?

Proof for Umar's Caliphate from Abu Bakr's Appointment
Proof for Umar's imamah based on Abu Bakr's appointment before the Companions.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the evidence that Imam Baqillani presents for Umar's caliphate, based on Abu Bakr's public appointment and description of Umar's qualities before the senior Companions.

Core Idea
Umar's caliphate is proven by Abu Bakr's public appointment and description.

In this section, Imam Baqillani responds to the question of what evidence establishes the caliphate of Umar ibn al-Khattab. He points to the actions of Abu Bakr, who appointed Umar in the presence of the senior Companions and publicly announced his choice, describing Umar's balanced character. Though the proof is not fully completed in this passage, the key elements of appointment and public declaration are clear.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Read the Arabic passage once without analysis, then read the literal translation to understand the flow of the argument.
The passage begins with a question-and-answer format.
2
Identify the four elements of proof
Look for the four elements listed in the commentary: (1) Abu Bakr giving precedence, (2) returning the decision to his own judgment, (3) public announcement, (4) sermon describing Umar's qualities.
These form the structure of the evidence.
3
Note the incomplete nature
The passage ends mid-sentence; the full argument likely continues. Focus on what is presented as the initial evidence.
This is a partial proof; a complete understanding may require subsequent pages.
4
Reflect on the significance
Consider why a public appointment in front of the Companions is considered strong evidence. How does this address questions about legitimacy?
This relates to broader debates about succession.

باب الكلام في إمامة عمر رضي الله عنه إن قال قائل : ما الدليل على إثبات إمامة عُمَر ؟ قيل له : الدليل على ذلك أن أبا بكر عهد إليه بمحضرٍ من جلّةِ الصحابة بعد تقدمه إليهم وأمره بالنظر في أمورهم والتشاور في إمامتهم وردّهم الأمر إلى نظره ورأيه، فقال: سأخبركم باختياري وخرج معصوباً رأسه فخطب خطبته المشهورة فوصف فيها عمر بصفاته ونعته بأخلاقه وذكر شـدته في غير عنف ولينه من غير ضعف
Chapter on the Speech Concerning the Imamate of Umar, may Allah be pleased with him. If a questioner says: What is the evidence for establishing the imamate of Umar? It is said to him: The evidence for that is that Abu Bakr appointed him in the presence of the senior Companions, after he had given them precedence and commanded him to look into their affairs and consult about their imamate, and he returned the matter to his view and opinion. He said: 'I will inform you of my choice.' He went out with his head bandaged and delivered his famous sermon in which he described Umar with his attributes and characterized him by his qualities, and mentioned his severity without harshness and his leniency without weakness.
Source pages p. 500

Commentary
This passage begins the section on Umar's caliphate by presenting the proof: Umar became caliph through the appointment (عهد) of Abu Bakr, done openly before the senior Companions. The proof rests on four elements: (1) Abu Bakr gave precedence to the Companions and instructed them to consult, (2) he then returned the decision to his own judgment, (3) he announced his choice publicly, and (4) he delivered a sermon describing Umar's qualities—severity without harshness and leniency without weakness. The passage does not complete the proof; it only states the initial evidence of appointment and the public announcement.

عهد
إمامة
صحابة
شورى

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Umar's caliphate lacked a clear appointment and was based solely on consultation or force.
Correction: This passage demonstrates that Umar was explicitly appointed by Abu Bakr in the presence of senior Companions, providing a clear chain of authority.

Checkpoint
What is the primary piece of evidence given for Umar's imamate in this passage?
A) Umar's own military conquests.
B) Abu Bakr's appointment of him in front of senior Companions.
C) The Ansar's choice of Umar.
D) A direct revelation from the Prophet Muhammad.

Key Takeaway
Abu Bakr's public appointment of Umar before the senior Companions, along with his descriptive sermon, provides the foundational evidence for Umar's caliphate.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Abu Bakr described Umar with 'severity without harshness and leniency without weakness.' Which of these two qualities is more lacking in your own character, and what one concrete step can you take today to begin correcting that imbalance?
?
Umar was appointed in front of witnesses. Who is watching your choices today? If you truly believed that every action is seen by Allah and recorded by the angels, what would you change about how you live this week?
?
The Companions deferred to Abu Bakr's judgment even after being asked to consult. When was the last time you humbly accepted someone else's decision over your own opinion for the sake of unity? What held you back, and how can you overcome that obstacle?

Baqillani's Defense of Abu Bakr's Imamate through Umar's Words
Baqillani explains Umar's remarks and concludes Abu Bakr's rightful imamate.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how Imam Baqillani interprets Umar's remarks to affirm Abu Bakr's rightful caliphate and refute objections.

Core Idea
Umar's words actually prove, not undermine, Abu Bakr's superiority.

This passage addresses an objection raised by those who cite Umar's statement about the caliphate being a 'sudden affair' to argue against Abu Bakr. Imam Baqillani carefully explains each phrase from Umar, showing they affirm Abu Bakr's preeminence and the legitimacy of his imamate. The lesson will walk through Baqillani's reasoning.

Guided Path
1
Read the objection and Baqillani's opening answer
First, read the objection posed by opponents: 'What is the meaning of the report?' Then read Baqillani's response that Umar believed Abu Bakr was the best of the ummah.
Notice how Baqillani starts by stating Umar's positive view of Abu Bakr.
2
Understand Umar's belief about Abu Bakr
Baqillani asserts that Umar considered Abu Bakr the most excellent, preeminent in virtue, and deserving of the caliphate through his merit. Those after him were close in rank, so Umar made it a shura among six.
This sets the stage for interpreting Umar's later remarks.
3
Analyze the three key phrases from Umar
Baqillani explains three statements: 'It was a sudden affair' (kānat faltatan), 'Allah spared its evil', and 'Whoever returns to something like it, kill him.' Each is given a meaning that supports Abu Bakr.
Pay attention to Baqillani's two possible interpretations for the third statement.
4
See how Baqillani concludes the argument
After explaining Umar's words, Baqillani concludes that the opponents' argument collapses and Abu Bakr's imamate is established.
This shows the power of proper interpretation in theological debate.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فإن قالوا فما معنى الخبر؟ قيل لهم : إن عُمَرَ كان يعتقد أن أبا بكر كان أفضل الأمة ومُبَرّزاً فيهم بالفضل وغير مُشتكل الأمر وأنه كان يستحق أخذها بالمناظرة عليها وأن من بعدها متقاربون في الرتبة والفضل لا يستحقونها على ذلك الوجه ؛ ولذلك جعلها شورى في ستة . وقوله «كانت فلتة» أي تمت على غير إعمال فكر ولا رويَّةٍ بل استوثقت فجاءةٌ. وقوله «وقى الله شرها»، يعني شر الخلاف عليها وشقّ العصا عند تمامها فإنه بعيد عنده أن ذلك مع ما رأى من تواثب الأنصار عليها واطلاع الفتنة رأسها وقوله «فمن عاد إلى مثلها فاقتلوه إنما أراد إلى مثل قول الأنصار وما حُكِيَ عن الأنصار من إرادتهم نصب إمامين في وقت واحد بقولهم: «منا أمير ومنكم أمير» ولإخراجهم الأمر من قريش إلى غيرهم وهذان الأمران حرام فعلهما في الدين وجالبان الفتنة وإنما عَظَّمَ غلط الأنصار فيهما فقال لأهل الشورى وغيرهم لما عهد إليهم فيها : إن من عاد إلى مثل قول الأنصار فاقتلوه ويمكن أن يكون أراد من حاول أخذها بالمناظرة عليها وإظهار التقدم والتبريز بالفضل على وجه ما فعله أبو بكر وعُرف ذلك من أمره فاقتلوه ؛ لأنه لم يبق في هذه الأمة هذه منزلته . وإذا كان كذلك سقط ما تعلقوا به صح بهذه الجملة إمامة أبي بكر رضي الله عنه ونضّر وجهه.
If they say: What is the meaning of the report? It is said to them: Indeed, Umar believed that Abu Bakr was the best of the ummah and preeminent among them in virtue and his matter was not ambiguous, and that he deserved to take it (the caliphate) by disputation over it, and that those after him were close in rank and virtue and did not deserve it in that manner; therefore he made it a consultation (shura) among six. And his statement 'It was a sudden affair' (kānat faltatan) means it was completed without prior reflection or deliberation, but rather it was established suddenly. And his statement 'Allah spared its evil' means the evil of dispute over it and the breaking of the stick (of unity) at its completion, for it was far from him that that (would happen) considering what he saw of the Anṣār's rushing upon it and the emergence of sedition at its peak. And his statement 'Whoever returns to something like it, kill him' – he only meant something like the statement of the Anṣār and what was reported from them of their desire to appoint two imams at one time by their saying: 'An amir from us and an amir from you,' and their removal of the matter from Quraysh to others. These two matters are forbidden to do in the religion and bring about sedition. He only exaggerated the error of the Anṣār in them, so he said to the people of the shura and others when he entrusted the matter to them: 'Whoever returns to something like the statement of the Anṣār, kill him.' And it is possible that he meant whoever tries to take it (the caliphate) by disputation and showing precedence and preeminence in virtue in the manner that Abu Bakr did and that was known from his affair, then kill him, because there is no one remaining in this nation with his rank. And if that is so, what they clung to falls, and by this summary the imamate of Abu Bakr, may Allah be pleased with him and brighten his face, is established.
Source pages p. 500

Commentary
This passage is an objection-and-answer followed by a conclusion. The author addresses an objection raised by opponents who appeal to a report from Umar to undermine Abu Bakr's imamate. The objection asks: 'What is the meaning of the report?' The answer explains that Umar's words actually affirm Abu Bakr's superior merit. Umar believed Abu Bakr was the most excellent of the community, unmistakably preeminent, and that he rightfully obtained the caliphate through his recognized merit (by disputation, meaning by virtue of his qualifications that were evident). Those after him were roughly equal in rank and thus not deserving in the same way; hence Umar made the matter a shura among six. The author then interprets three specific statements of Umar: (1) 'It was a sudden affair' (kānat faltatan) means it was done without prior deliberation but suddenly succeeded—not that it was wrong. (2) 'Allah spared its evil' refers to the evil of conflict and division that would have occurred had it not been for Allah's protection at that moment. (3) 'Whoever returns to something like it, kill him' has two possible meanings: either it refers to the Anṣār's attempt to appoint two imams simultaneously and to remove the caliphate from Quraysh—both actions are forbidden and cause fitna—or it refers to anyone trying to claim the caliphate by disputation and displaying merit in the manner of Abu Bakr, because no one else had his rank. Having clarified Umar's words, the author concludes that the opponents' argument collapses, and the imamate of Abu Bakr is established.

Key Terms
فلتة (faltatan: sudden affair)
شورى (shura: consultation)
تواثب (tawathub: rushing)
فتنة (fitna: sedition)

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Umar's phrase 'kānat faltatan' is often taken as criticism of Abu Bakr's caliphate being illegitimate or a mistake.
Correction: Baqillani explains that 'faltatan' simply describes the speed and lack of prior deliberation, not illegitimacy. Umar affirmed Abu Bakr's merit.

Checkpoint
According to Imam Baqillani, what did Umar mean by calling Abu Bakr's caliphate a 'فلتة' (sudden affair)?
A) He meant it was illegitimate.
B) He meant it occurred without prior deliberation but was sound.
C) He meant it was a mistake.
D) He meant it was forced upon the people.

Key Takeaway
Baqillani's exegesis shows that Umar's words, when properly understood, support rather than undermine Abu Bakr's imamate.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you read a report that seems critical of a respected figure like Abu Bakr, do you immediately accept the surface meaning or do you seek a deeper understanding like Baqillani did? What does your reaction reveal about your trust in the Companions and your method of studying history? This week, commit to reading one controversial report with the intention to understand it in light of broader Islamic principles, not just the literal wording.
?
Baqillani’s interpretation of Umar’s words required careful attention to context. Think of a time you misunderstood someone’s words because you ignored context. Did that lead to unfair judgment? How can you apply Baqillani’s approach—seeking the intended meaning by considering the speaker’s beliefs and the situation—to avoid such mistakes in the future? Decide on one concrete step to practice this before responding to someone you disagree with.
?
This lesson shows that Umar’s words actually affirm Abu Bakr’s superiority. Does your heart fully accept the legitimacy and order of the first caliph, or are there lingering doubts? If there are, what are they based on—incomplete knowledge or cultural influences? Reflect on how Baqillani’s argument strengthens your conviction, and ask Allah to grant you certainty. Then, write down one way you can actively defend this truth in your circle, using evidence from the sources.

The Proof for Umar's Imamate
Imam Baqillani presents proof for Umar's imamate via appointment and consensus.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the structured proof that Imam Baqillani uses to establish the legitimacy of Umar's caliphate through Abu Bakr's explicit appointment and the subsequent acceptance by senior Companions, especially Talha.

Core Idea
Umar's imamate is validated by explicit appointment and confirmed by those who initially objected.

This passage presents a key argument from Sunni kalam for the legitimacy of Umar's caliphate. It responds to potential objections by grounding the proof in historical events witnessed by the senior Companions. The argument is structured as a question and answer, making it clear that the evidence is not just political but based on the consensus of the community after the initial appointment.

Guided Path
1
Identify the structure
Notice that the passage begins with a hypothetical question: 'What is the proof for ʿUmar's imamate?' The answer that follows forms the entire proof. This question-and-answer format is typical in kalam works to address objections.
2
Study Abu Bakr's appointment
Read how Abu Bakr appointed ʿUmar in the presence of the senior Companions after they referred the matter back to him. Note that he delivered a famous sermon describing ʿUmar's qualities.
Pay attention to the description: severity without harshness, leniency without weakness.
3
Examine Talha's objection and response
Talha initially objects, calling ʿUmar harsh. Abu Bakr defends his choice firmly, rebuking Talha and stating he appointed the best of Allah's people. This shows Abu Bakr's confidence.
Abu Bakr's strong response indicates the certainty of the appointment.
4
Note Talha's later endorsement
Later, when ʿUmar consulted about the Nihāwand campaign, Talha praised ʿUmar's leadership and expressed full confidence. This endorsement from a former objector strengthens the proof.
Talha's change of heart shows the legitimacy was universally recognized.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
باب الكلام في إمامة عمر رضي الله عنه
إن قال قائل : ما الدليل على إثبات إمامة عُمَر ؟ قيل له : الدليل على ذلك أن أبا بكر عهد إليه بمحضرٍ من جلّةِ الصحابة بعد تقدمه إليهم وأمره بالنظر في أمورهم والتشاور في إمامتهم وردّهم الأمر إلى نظره ورأيه، فقال: سأخبركم باختياري وخرج معصوباً رأسه فخطب خطبته المشهورة فوصف فيها عمر بصفاته ونعته بأخلاقه وذكر شـدته في غير عنف ولينه من غير ضعف وقدرته على الأمر ؛ ثم أجاب طلحة لما قال له : «تولي علينا فظاً غليظاً، ماذا تقول لربك إذا لقيته؟» : «قد فركت لي عينيك ودلكت لي عقبيك وجئتني تلفتني عن رأيي وتصدني عن ديني ؛ والله لتتركن عضيهته أو لأنفينك في كلام له طويل أقول إذا سألني : وليت عليهم خير أهلك» (۱) ثم قال: «والله لتألمُنَّ النوم على الصوف الأذربي كما يألم أحدكم النوم على حسك السعدان يا هادي الطريق جزت إنما هو البحرُ أو الفجر ) (۲) في كلام له قد ذكرناه في غير هذا الموضع .
وقد اعترف طلحة بصواب رأيه ووصف عمر لما شاورهم بالخروج بنفسه إلى ملوك نهاوند بما (۳) وصفه أبو بكر وفوقه وقال له في كلام مشهور: «لقد استقامت العرب عليك وفتح الله على يديك فسر بنـا فـإنا لا نستعصي عليك» (٤) وما هذا معناه من قول طلحة وقد قال طلحة وعثمان وعبد الرحمن
(۱) انظر طبقات ابن سعد ۱۹۹/۳.
(۲) هو من قول أبي بكر مما حدث عبد الرحمن بن عوف عنه . انظر الكامل للمبرد ٥/١ وقوله على الصوف الأذربي فهذا منسوب إلى أذربيجان وقوله على حسك السعدان فالسعدان نبت كثير الحسك تأكله الإبل فتسمن عليه ويغذوها غذاء لا يوجد في غيره. وقوله إنما هو والله الفجر والبحر يقول إن انتظرت حتى يضيء لك الفجر الطريق أبصرت قصدك وإن خبطت الظلماء وركبت العشواء هجمابك على المكروه. وضرب ذلك مثلاً لغمرات الدنيا وتهجيرها أهلها . (۳) نهاوند بفتح النون الأولى وتكسر وهي مدينة عظيمة : هي مدينة عظيمة في قبلة همذان بينهما ثلاثة أيام قيل أصلها بنو هاوند فاختصروا منها ومعناه الخير المضاعف وكان فتحها سنة ١٩ ويقال سنة ٢٠ ، وذكر أبو بكر الهذلي عن محمد بن الحسن كانت وقعة نهاوند سنة ٢١ أيام عمر بن الخطاب رضي الله عنه وأمير المسلمين النعمان بن مقرن المزني، وقال عمر: إن أصبت فالأمير حذيفة بن اليمان ثم جرير بن عبد الله ثم المغيرة بن شعبة ثم الأشعث بن قيس، فقتل النعمان وكان صحابياً فأخذ الراية حذيفة وكان الفتح على يده صلحاً. انظر معجم البلدان ۳۱۳/٥ باب النون والهاء وما يليهما . (٤) ذكر ابن الأثير في الكامل ۷/۳ قول طلحة لعمر ما نصه : يا أمير المؤمنين قد أحكمتك الأمور، وعجمتك البلابل واحتنكتك التجارب وأنت وشأنك ورأيك لا ننبوا في يديك ولا نكل عليك إليك هذا الأمر، فمرنا نطع وادعنا نجب واحملنا نركب وقدنا ننقذ فإنك ولي هذا الأمر، وقد بلوت وجربت واحتريت فلم ينكشف شيء من عواقب قضاء الله لك إلا عن خيارهم . وهي أيضاً في الرياض النضرة ٢٦٣/٤ في مناقب طلحة في ذكر أنه كان خطباء الصحابة .
Chapter on the discourse concerning the imamate of ʿUmar, may Allah be pleased with him.
If someone says: What is the proof for establishing the imamate of ʿUmar? It is said to him: The proof for that is that Abu Bakr appointed him in the presence of the senior Companions after he had presented himself to them and commanded him to look into their affairs and to consult regarding their imamate, and they referred the matter back to his view and opinion. He said: 'I will inform you of my choice.' He came out with his head bandaged and delivered his famous sermon in which he described ʿUmar with his attributes and characterized him by his qualities, mentioning his severity without harshness, his leniency without weakness, and his capability over the matter. Then he answered Ṭalḥa when he said to him: 'You appoint over us a coarse harsh man; what will you say to your Lord when you meet Him?' (He replied): 'You have rubbed my eyes and massaged my heels for me, and you come to me turning me away from my opinion and diverting me from my religion; by Allah, you will leave your insolence or I will banish you...' in a lengthy speech of his, saying: 'When He asks me, I will say: I appointed over them the best of Your people.' (1) Then he said: 'By Allah, you will experience sleeping on Azerbaijani wool as one of you experiences sleeping on the thorns of saʿdān... O guide of the path, you have crossed; it is only the sea or the dawn...' (2) in a speech of his that we have mentioned elsewhere.
And Ṭalḥa acknowledged the correctness of his opinion and described ʿUmar when he consulted them about going out himself to the kings of Nihāwand with what (3) Abu Bakr had described and more. He said to him in famous speech: 'The Arabs have become steady under you and Allah has opened (conquests) at your hands, so proceed with us, for we do not rebel against you.' (4) And this is the meaning of the statement of Ṭalḥa, and Ṭalḥa, ʿUthmān, and ʿAbd al-Raḥmān said...
(1) See Ṭabaqāt Ibn Saʿd, 3/199.
(2) It is from the saying of Abu Bakr from what ʿAbd al-Raḥmān ibn ʿAwf narrated from him. See al-Kāmil of al-Mubarrad, 5/1. And his saying 'on Azerbaijani wool' is attributed to Azerbaijan. And his saying 'on the thorns of saʿdān' – saʿdān is a plant with many thorns which camels eat and fatten on, and it nourishes them with nourishment not found in others. And his saying 'it is only, by Allah, the dawn and the sea' means: If you wait until the dawn illuminates the path for you, you will see your goal; but if you stumble in the darkness and ride blindly, it will throw you into misfortune. He made this a metaphor for the tribulations of the world and its troubling of its people.
(3) Nihāwand, with the first nun opened and it is kasra [i.e., it is also broken?], is a great city: it is a great city in the qibla of Hamadhān, between them three days. It is said its origin is Banū Hāwand, so they abbreviated from it, and its meaning is multiplied good. Its conquest was in the year 19, and it is said year 20. And Abu Bakr al-Hudhalī mentioned from Muḥammad ibn al-Ḥasan that the battle of Nihāwand was in the year 21 during the days of ʿUmar ibn al-Khaṭṭāb, may Allah be pleased with him, and the commander of the Muslims was al-Nuʿmān ibn Muqarrin al-Muzanī. And ʿUmar said: If I am hit, then the commander is Ḥudhayfa ibn al-Yamān, then Jarīr ibn ʿAbd Allāh, then al-Mughīra ibn Shuʿba, then al-Ashʿath ibn Qays. So al-Nuʿmān was killed, and he was a Companion, so Ḥudhayfa took the banner, and the conquest was by truce at his hand. See Muʿjam al-Buldān, 5/313, chapter on nūn and hā and what follows.
(4) Ibn al-Athīr mentioned in al-Kāmil, 7/3, the statement of Ṭalḥa to ʿUmar, the text of which is: O Commander of the Faithful, matters have made you wise, calamities have tested you, and experiences have seasoned you. You are your own concern and your opinion; we do not recoil in your hands nor tire of you. This matter is yours, so command us and we obey, call us and we respond, carry us and we ride, lead us and we follow, for you are the guardian of this matter. You have tested and tried and investigated, and nothing of the outcomes of Allah's decree for you has been revealed except as the best of them. And it is also in al-Riyāḍ al-Nāḍira, 4/263, in the virtues of Ṭalḥa, mentioning that he was among the orators of the Companions.
Source pages p. 500

Commentary
This passage is a proof (dalīl) for the imamate of ʿUmar ibn al-Khaṭṭāb. The author presents the evidence in the form of a question-and-answer: someone asks for the proof of ʿUmar's imamate, and the answer is given. The proof has two main components: the direct appointment by Abu Bakr in the presence of senior Companions, and the subsequent endorsement by key figures like Ṭalḥa.

First, the author states that Abu Bakr formally appointed ʿUmar in the presence of the senior Companions after he (Abu Bakr) had previously addressed them and commanded them to look into their own affairs and consult about the imamate, but they referred the matter back to him. Abu Bakr then announced his choice publicly while bandaged (due to illness), delivering a sermon in which he praised ʿUmar's qualities: his severity without harshness, his leniency without weakness, and his capability.

Second, when Ṭalḥa objected, calling ʿUmar harsh and coarse, Abu Bakr defended his choice firmly, rebuking Ṭalḥa and stating that when Allah asks him, he will say he appointed the best of His people. This shows Abu Bakr's confidence and the legitimacy of the choice.

Third, the author cites Ṭalḥa's later acknowledgment: when ʿUmar consulted the Companions about leading the army himself against the kings of Nihāwand, Ṭalḥa expressed full confidence in ʿUmar's leadership, stating that the Arabs had become steady under him and that they would not rebel against him. This testimony from Ṭalḥa, who had earlier questioned the appointment, validates the choice.

The passage also includes extensive footnotes (likely from the editor) providing references and explanations of terms like 'Azerbaijani wool' (soft wool) and 'thorns of saʿdān' (painful), illustrating metaphors in Abu Bakr's speech. The footnote about Nihāwand gives historical details of the conquest. All these support the author's argument that ʿUmar's imamate was established by Abu Bakr's designation and confirmed by the companions' acceptance.

Key Terms
عهد (ʿahd: appointment)
جلّة الصحابة (jillat al-ṣaḥāba: senior Companions)
شورى (shura: consultation)
صفات (ṣifāt: attributes)
نهاوند (Nihāwand: a city)

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Umar's caliphate was merely a political choice without divine guidance or merit.
Correction: The passage shows it was based on an explicit appointment by Abu Bakr, who was guided by his knowledge of Umar's qualities, and later confirmed by the consensus of the senior Companions, including those who initially questioned it.

Checkpoint
Who initially objected to ʿUmar's appointment, and how did he later show his acceptance?
A) ʿUthmān questioned it, and later he gave allegiance.
B) Ṭalḥa called ʿUmar harsh, and later praised his leadership during the Nihāwand consultation.
C) ʿAbd al-Raḥmān ibn ʿAwf objected, and later he apologized.
D) The senior Companions all agreed immediately.

Key Takeaway
The imamate of ʿUmar is proven by the explicit appointment of Abu Bakr and the subsequent acceptance by the senior Companions, demonstrating both designation and consensus.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When Talha initially objected to Umar's appointment, he saw only harshness. Is there a leader in your life—a parent, teacher, or imam—whom you have judged too harshly? Could it be that you are missing the very qualities that make them the right choice for you? Will you ask Allah to open your heart to see their strengths as Abu Bakr did?
?
The senior Companions accepted Umar even after an initial objection. Are there people in your community whose leadership you have resisted because of one flaw? What would it take for you to recognise, as Talha did, that the stability of the group depends on your support? Will you actively seek to reconcile with a leader you have opposed?
?
Abu Bakr did not back down when challenged; he defended his choice with conviction. Are you firm in your commitment to the truth, or do you waver when others criticise? In what area of your faith do you need to stand firm like Abu Bakr, trusting that Allah guides the affair?

The Validity of the Imam Appointing a Successor
Al-Baqillani's primary proof for the validity of appointment.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the main arguments used by al-Baqillani to prove that an Imam has the right to appoint his successor, including the silence of the Companions, consensus, and an analogy.

Core Idea
An Imam's right to appoint is proven by precedent, consensus, and logical analogy.

Al-Baqillani begins by addressing an objection: why does the Imam appoint when God has not explicitly commanded it? He argues that the Companions did not object to Abu Bakr's appointment of Umar, which would have been unthinkable if it were wrong. He then cites the consensus of the people of selection (Ahl al-Ikhtiyar) and uses an analogy: if a just non-Imam can initiate a contract for imamate, the Imam retains the same right.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage once without trying to analyse it. Then read the translation. Let the author's own rhythm come through before you interpret.
Notice that Baqillani uses a very compressed style here.
2
Identify the three arguments
The passage presents three main proofs: the silence of the Companions, the consensus of Ahl al-Ikhtiyar, and an analogy with a just non-Imam. Find each one and notice how Baqillani presents them.
3
Reflect on the strength of the analogy
Ask yourself why the analogy is effective. Baqillani argues that the Imam's status does not diminish his right to contract; in fact, it may enhance it.
This connects to the learning objective.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
يقل قائل منهم : لِمَ تعهدُ في أمر ما جعل الله لك العهد فيه؟ ولا قال ذلك قائل في غير مجلسه ولا بعد وفاته ولو كان عهده إلى عمر خطأ في الدين لسارعوا إلى تعريفه ذلك ومواقفته عليه ولكان أجدر من قول قائلهم : علينا فظاً غليظاً؟ إذ كان ليس له أن يولي عليهم أحداً لا فظاً ولا رفيقاً وكان [؟] تنبيهه على ذلك واد كـاره به ومطالبته بتركه أولى من خوضهم في صفة يعهد إليه ، لأن الكلام في صفة من يعهد إليه فرع للكلام في صفة العهد أولا : وإذا لم يصح العهد جمله سقط الخوض فيه في صفة المعهود إليه وزالت المؤونة ومثل هذا الخطأ والتفريط الظاهر لا يجوز على كافة لمسلمين وقادة الأنصار والمهاجرين؛ لأن الأمة لن تجتمع في عصر عصر الصحابة ولا في غيره على خطأ وإمساك عن إنكار ما من سبيله أن يُنكر، حتى لا يكون فيها إلا متدين بصحة العهد من الإمام إلى غيره وقائل به ومصوبٌ له، لأن القول بالعهد وفعله خطأ من فاعله الرّضي به والإقرار له خطأ من المقر له، إذ كان العهد خطأ في الدين والأمة لا تجتمع على خطأ. ويدل عليه أيضاً إجماع أهل الاختيار الذين هم أهل الحق، في القول بالإمامة : أن للإمام أن يعهد إلى إمام بعده ولسنا نعرف منهم من ينكر ذلك ولا يثبت عن أحد منهم برواية شاذة ومقالة مرويَّةٍ أنه لم يكن قائلاً بها ولا ذاهباً إليها . ويدل على ذلك أيضاً ويوضحه علمنا أن الإمام العدل لو لم يكن إماماً وكان رجلاً من الرعية لكان له أن يبتدىء العقد لمن يصلح للإمامة وإذا كان ذلك كذلك فكونه إماماً لا يحطّه عن هذه الرتبة فوجب أن يكون له أن يعقد على إمام بعده ويعهد إليه كما كان له أن يبتدىء العقد له لأن العقد في الحقيقة عقد على صفة فصح بذلك ما قلناه . فإن قال قائل : فما أنكرتم من تحريم العهد من الإمام لغيره لموضع التهمة من العاهد وتجويز ميله إلى المعهود إليه وإيثاره لولايته ؛ قيل له هذه التهمة معصية الله ممن جناها وظنها بإمام المسلمين إذا كان عفيفاً مشهوراً ظاهر العدالة منصفاً للأمة لم تكن منه خيانة لهم في مدة أيام نظره ولا مخاتلة ولا جبرية فهو بالاً يتهم بعد الموت ويحتقب عظيم الإثم في تسليط ظالم عليهم أو جاهل بأمورهم أولى وفي هذا ما يوجب أن يكون ظن المسلمين بإمامهم الذي لم يعرفوه إلا بالصلاح والاستقامة والتهمة له ذنباً التوبة والاستغفار منه تجب ولا يجوز أن يبطل العهد منه إلى من عهد إليه، وإن كان ممن يصلح أن يبتدىء العقد على غيره لأجل هذه التهمة وعلى أن هذا المعنى قائم في العاقد كوجوده في العاهد فيجب أيضاً أن يبطل عقد العاقد لغيره، لأنـه قد يجوز أن يعقل لمن يميل إلى نظره ويؤثر ولايته ويرجو الاعتداد والانتفاع به مع العلم بأنه غير مقصر في هذا الشأن فلما لم يجز إبطال العقد بهذه التهمة لم يجز إبطال العهد. فصحت بهذه الجملة إمامة عمر رضي الله عنه وأنه بصفة من يصلح العهد إليه وابتداء العقد له وكان العاقد لـه إماماً عدلاً رضى بصفة من له أن يعهد إلى غيره.
A speaker among them says: 'Why do you appoint in a matter in which God has not given you the authority to appoint?' And no one said that in his lifetime or after his death. And if his appointment of Umar were an error in religion, they would have hurried to inform him of that and confront him with it, and it would have been more deserving than their saying: 'Rough and harsh upon us,' since he had no right to appoint over them anyone rough nor gentle. And [؟] reminding him of that and urging him to abandon it would have been more befitting than their delving into the character of the one appointed, because speech about the character of the one appointed is subsidiary to speech about the character of the appointment first: and if the appointment as a whole is invalid, then delving into the character of the appointee becomes moot and the burden is removed. And such manifest error and negligence is not permissible for the entirety of Muslims and the leaders of the Ansar and Muhajirun, because the community does not unite in any era, the era of the Companions or otherwise, upon error and refraining from denouncing what must be denounced, such that there would be none among them except one who adheres to the validity of the appointment from the Imam to another and speaks it and considers it correct. Because speaking and acting upon the appointment is an error from its doer, and being pleased with it and affirming it is an error from the one who affirms it, since the appointment is an error in religion, and the community does not unite upon error. Also evidence for it is the consensus of the people of selection (Ahl al-Ikhtiyar) who are the people of truth, regarding the statement on imamate: that the Imam may appoint an Imam after him, and we do not know of anyone among them who denies that, nor is it established from any of them through an isolated narration or a reported saying that he did not hold it or adhere to it. Also evidence for that and clarifying it is our knowledge that if the just Imam were not an Imam and were a man from the subjects, he would have the right to initiate the contract for one who is suitable for imamate. And if that is the case, then his being an Imam does not lower him from this rank, so it is necessary that he have the right to contract for an Imam after him and appoint him just as he had the right to initiate the contract for him, because the contract in reality is a contract upon a qualification. Thus what we have said is proven. Then if a questioner says: 'What prevents you from prohibiting the appointment by the Imam to another due to suspicion from the appointor and the possibility of his inclination toward the appointee and preference for his authority?' It is said to him: This suspicion is disobedience to God from whoever commits it and suspects the Imam of the Muslims when he is chaste, well-known, manifestly just, fair to the community, there has been no betrayal from him during his period of oversight, nor deceit nor coercion. So how can he be suspected after death and incur great sin by imposing a tyrant or an ignorant person upon them? It is more appropriate that the suspicion of the Muslims toward their Imam, whom they have only known as righteous and upright, be a sin for which repentance and seeking forgiveness are obligatory. And it is not permissible to invalidate the appointment from him to the one he appointed, even if he is one who is suitable to initiate the contract for someone else, because of this suspicion. Moreover, this meaning exists in the contractor just as it exists in the appointor, so it would also be necessary to invalidate the contract of the contractor for someone else, because he might contract for someone he inclines to and prefers his authority and hopes for advancement and benefit, while knowing that he is not deficient in this matter. So when it is not permissible to invalidate the contract due to this suspicion, it is not permissible to invalidate the appointment. Thus, by this totality, the imamate of Umar, may God be pleased with him, is established, and that he is of the description of one suitable for appointment and initiation of contract for him, and the contractor for him was a just Imam who was pleased with the description of one who has the right to appoint to another.
Source pages p. 508

Commentary
This passage is a multi-part argument for the validity of an Imam appointing his successor. Al-Baqillani first addresses a hypothetical objector who questions the Imam's authority to appoint. He argues that if Umar's appointment were an error, the Companions would have denounced it; since they did not, it must be correct. He then cites consensus (ijma') of the Ahl al-Ikhtiyar that the Imam may appoint. Next, he uses an analogy: a just non-Imam may initiate a contract for imamate, so the Imam, who is not lower in rank, retains this right. Then he refutes the objection of suspicion (tuhma): to suspect a just Imam is a sin, and the same suspicion would apply to the initial contract, so if that contract is valid, the appointment is also valid. Finally, he concludes that Umar's imamate is established and that the contractor was a just Imam who had the right to appoint.

Key Terms
العهد
الإمامة
الإجماع
أهل الاختيار

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: The Imam cannot appoint a successor because God did not explicitly command it.
Correction: Baqillani shows that the Companions accepted Abu Bakr's appointment of Umar, so it is valid; consensus and analogy further support it.

Checkpoint
What does al-Baqillani use as evidence for the validity of the Imam's appointment?
A) Explicit Quranic text
B) Consensus of Ahl al-Ikhtiyar
C) Analogy with a just non-Imam
D) Both B and C

Key Takeaway
The Imam's right to appoint a successor is supported by the silence of the Companions, consensus, and a logical analogy.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you remain silent about a religious matter, do you ever consider that your silence might be seen as approval? Think of a time you stayed quiet about something that needed correction. Write down what you will do next time.
?
Al-Baqillani argues that the community cannot unite on error. Where in your own life do you rely on the consensus of trustworthy people rather than your own limited understanding? Is that reliance genuine or lazy?
?
The objector asked 'Why do you appoint?' as if to demand divine authorization. Are there areas in your spiritual life where you demand explicit proof before obeying, while ignoring the cumulative wisdom of those who came before you? Repent of that demand today.

Refuting the Suspicion Objection to Appointment
Refutation of the suspicion objection and conclusion.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how al-Baqillani refutes the claim that suspicion of bias invalidates the Imam's appointment.

Core Idea
Suspicion of bias does not invalidate an appointment because it would also invalidate the initial contract.

Al-Baqillani now addresses a second objection: that the Imam might be biased toward the appointee. He argues that leveling such suspicion against a just Imam is a sin, and furthermore, the same suspicion could be applied to the original contract choosing the Imam himself. Since that contract is valid, the appointment must also be valid.

Guided Path
1
Read the objection and response
Read the Arabic passage and translation, focusing on the structure: first the objection, then the Imam's response.
Notice the two parts of the response: the sin of suspicion and the parity argument.
2
Understand the parity argument
Al-Baqillani says that the same suspicion exists in the initial contract, so if we invalidate the appointment, we must also invalidate the contract. Since the contract is accepted, the appointment must stand.
3
Connect to the overall conclusion
The passage ends with establishing Umar's imamate, tying the argument back to the historical example.
This shows the practical significance of the theoretical debate.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Suspicion of bias automatically invalidates an Imam's appointment.
Correction: Baqillani shows that such suspicion would also invalidate the initial contract, which is accepted. Therefore, suspicion cannot invalidate the appointment.

Checkpoint
Why does al-Baqillani say that suspicion does not invalidate the appointment?
A) Because the Imam is infallible
B) Because the same suspicion would invalidate the initial contract
C) Because the appointee is proven just
D) Because the companions did not object

Key Takeaway
Suspicion of bias cannot invalidate an appointment without also invalidating the very process that established the Imam.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When have you harbored suspicion against a leader in your community without clear evidence? How does the lesson's warning about the sin of suspicion challenge you to repent and change your attitude?
?
The argument shows that the same measure you apply to others must also apply to yourself. Is there a relationship or decision where you have been quick to suspect another's motives, while ignoring your own potential biases? What would it look like to apply consistent standards?
?
If you were in a position of trust (parent, teacher, employer), how would this lesson affect the way you handle accusations of favoritism? Would you be willing to defend your decisions based on the same logical consistency, or would you let suspicion of others shape your actions?

Evidence for Uthman's Imamate: The Shura and Bay'ah
Evidence from shura and Talha's bay'ah

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how the shura conducted by Abd al-Rahman ibn Awf and Talha's subsequent bay'ah serve as evidence for Uthman's imamate.

Core Idea
The shura and unanimous consent confirm Uthman's rightful imamate.

Al-Baqillani begins his defense of Uthman's imamate by citing the historical process that led to his selection. He points to the shura organized by Umar and executed by Abd al-Rahman ibn Awf, which resulted in Uthman's appointment. The later bay'ah of Talha, who was initially absent, further confirms the community's acceptance.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage on shura and bay'ah
Read the Arabic and translation focusing on the shura and Talha's bay'ah. Note the specific details: Abd al-Rahman ibn Awf contracted the imamate in the presence of the shura members except Talha, and Talha later gave bay'ah indicating his approval.
2
Analyze the logical structure
The passage presents two pieces of evidence: the shura itself and Talha's bay'ah. Ask why Talha's bay'ah is needed? Because his initial absence could be seen as objection, but his later oath confirms consensus.
3
Connect to broader context
Consider why al-Baqillani uses historical events rather than direct scriptural proof. This reflects the Sunni method of establishing imamate through qualified selection and community acceptance.
